[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2),
[treasures](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures), and magical
items. Once these
[dungeons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon) are
created the referee should mark them on his map somewhere in the
vicinity of the start of play. The
[campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign) is then
ready and the players can begin exploring the fantasy milieu in which
they find themselves.

### The Referee’s Supplies

In addition to those supplies recommended for players the referee should
furnish himself with the following:

#### The Essentials:

-   Delving Deeper (you have it!),
-   Polyhedral [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1)
    (two pair of six-sided
    [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) and one pair
    each of four-, eight-, ten-, twelve-, and twenty-sided
    [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1)),
-   A [campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign) log
    or notebook to [keep](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#keep)
    track of characters, places,
    [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2),
    non-player characters and
    [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2), and
    [treasures](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures),
-   A [campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign)
    calendar for timekeeping,
-   A creative mind and the ability to “run the show”.

#### Optional Extras:

-   Additional [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1)
    (with twenty-sided
    [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) optionally
    marked 0-9 twice),
-   Additional miniatures to represent
    [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2),
-   [Scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) models or maps of
    [dungeons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
    and
    [wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
    environs,
-   [Mass battles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#mass-battles)
    rules such as Chainmail, De Bellis Fantasticus, Book of War, or
    similar.

## Creating a World

The referee begins by creating a map of the world on a sheet of hex
paper. This map need not be extensive as exploration of the unknown is a
desired element of the
[campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign). It must,
however, remain unknown to the players.

Each hex should be 6 miles wide on this map such that an unencumbered
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) afoot can cover two hexes
per day of good hiking and an encumbered
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) can cover one hex per
day.

The referee should note at least one civilized
[settlement](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#settlements-and-strongholds_1)
(the village, town, or
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) where play
will begin) near the center of his map. He should then add any
immediately surrounding features including other villages, nearby towns,
a [keep](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#keep), a ruin, caves, a
forest, a swamp, and so on. The referee should name each feature and
decide whether it is abandoned or inhabited, and (if so) by whom?
Denizens might be ordinary lawful folk,
[elves](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elves_1),
[bandits](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men-bandits), a knight and
his entourage, [orcs](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#orcs),
[trolls](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#trolls), an evil high
priest, and so on. Thus the game world begins to take shape.

### The Start of Play

Play should commence in a (relatively) safe haven such as a town,
village, or
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds). Towns are
busy regional centers, home to 1,000-6,000 folk from all walks of life
including many itinerants. Villages are quiet, agrarian communities of
100-400 farming folk.
[Strongholds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) are
occupied by bodies of 30-180 soldiery along with a prominent leader and
his supporting entourage. Wherever they begin, players should be able to
acquire their starting goods and
[rumors](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#legend-and-rumors) of
possible adventures.

#### Legend and Rumors

The players might already know some of the
[campaign’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign) cultural
folklore. Other tales and local legends can be devised by the referee
and learned by the players as required.

The arrival or formation of a company of armed adventurers will not go
unnoticed and, unless the players take pains to conceal their purpose,
rumors will quickly spread. The players may, of course, desire to
advertise their presence in order to gain employment.

Obtaining news and rumors is thereafter a matter of visiting local inns
and common rooms where a liberal round of drinks worth 10-60 gp will
usually get tongues wagging, or where an earnest barkeep might be
willing to help for 1-6 gp. Misinformation may be learned at the
referee’s discretion.

#### Angry Villagers

In time the players might become fearless heroes (or feared
anti-heroes). This does not imply that exploitation of the common folk
will be without consequence. Unhappy commoners will first seek the
protection of the church and their local lords. Failing that they will
seek out a hero to fight their cause or, ultimately, rise up as an angry
lynch mob to run despots and villains out of town.

#### Hireling and Retainer Loyalty

Whenever [hirelings](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hirelings) or
[retainers](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainers) are taken on
the referee should secretly determine their
[loyalty](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainer-loyalty) score. A
[hireling](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hirelings) or
[retainer’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainers)
[loyalty](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainer-loyalty) score is
determined with a throw of three six-sided
[dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1), then adjusted
according to an initial
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
check (−2 to +2), the character’s
[loyalty](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainer-loyalty)
adjustment due to
[charisma](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#charisma) (−2 to +4), and
whether or not the
[hireling](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hirelings) or
[retainer](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainers) is a
disinherited [relative](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#relatives)
(0 to −5). The result is noted by the referee, to be referred to
whenever subsequent
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
or
[morale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
checks are required.

Delving Deeper Online table2\_1

|                                                    |                    |
|----------------------------------------------------|--------------------|
| Table 2.1 Loyalty                                  |                    |
|                                                    | Reaction or Morale |
| Loyalty                                            | Adjustment         |
| 3 or less                                          | \*                 |
| 4-5                                                | –2                 |
| 6-8                                                | –1                 |
| 9-12                                               | .                  |
| 13-15                                              | +1                 |
| 16-17                                              | +2                 |
| 18 or more                                         | \*\*               |
| \* Will betray or desert at the first opportunity. |                    |
| \*\* Will never betray or desert.                  |                    |

### The Dice

Delving Deeper referees require polyhedral dice of the four-, six-,
eight-, ten-, twelve-, and twenty-sided sorts and are assumed to possess
these.

Wherever number ranges appear in the text the referee should throw the
appropriate number of dice to produce a result within the specified
range. For example, a range of 1-6 is generated by throwing a six-sided
die, a range of 2-7 is generated by throwing a six-sided die and adding
1 to the result, a range of 2-10 is generated by throwing a six- and a
four-sided die and summing the results, and so on.

Common number ranges are given in the table below—the referee can
extrapolate other ranges from these examples. A ten-sided die should
ideally be a twenty-sided polyhedron marked 0-9 twice, but alternatively
can be a ten-sided polyhedron marked 0-9 once (although these are not a
platonic solid).

A range of 1-100 can be generated with a throw of two ten-sided dice.
The result of the first die is multiplied by ten before the pair is
summed. Thus, a throw of 4 and 2 makes 42, a throw of 6 and 0 makes 60,
and a throw of 0 and 6 makes 06. A double zero makes 100.

Delving Deeper Online table2\_2

|                                          |       |       |       |       |        |        |
|------------------------------------------|-------|-------|-------|-------|--------|--------|
| Table 2.2 Dice to Roll for Number Ranges |       |       |       |       |        |        |
| Number                                   | Four  | Six   | Eight | Ten   | Twelve | Twenty |
| of Dice                                  | Sided | Sided | Sided | Sided | Sided  | Sided  |
| 1                                        | 1-4   | 1-6   | 1-8   | 1-10  | 1-12   | 1-20   |
| 1+1                                      | 2-5   | 2-7   | 2-9   | 2-11  | 2-13   | 2-21   |
| 1+2                                      | 3-6   | 3-8   | 3-10  | 3-12  | 3-14   | 3-22   |
| 2                                        | 2-8   | 2-12  | 2-16  | 2-20  | 2-24   | 2-40   |
| 2+1                                      | 3-9   | 3-13  | 3-17  | 3-21  | 3-25   | 3-41   |
| 3                                        | 3-12  | 3-18  | 3-24  | 3-30  | 3-36   | 3-60   |

## Creating a Dungeon

Before the players can explore the labyrinthine
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration)
the referee must map at least one such
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon) on a
sheet of graph paper. A
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
should have many levels and sub-levels that are interconnected by
stairs, trapdoors, chutes, slanting passages, and so on. The referee is
advised to begin by drawing a cross section of the entire structure in
order to understand the means of egress between the various levels.

It is desirable that there be several
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
entrances, that there be a number routes between the various levels, and
that richer areas be harder to find. Deeper
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
levels will be more rewarding but also more dangerous, so players should
(usually) be allowed to navigate to the desired
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
level when such routes are known.

A [dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
need not be mapped completely—it may well be vast or even limitless. It
should, however, extend as far as the players are likely to explore in
their initial delve. Thus, the referee is advised to plan much of the
first level and some parts of the second and third levels. Each square
of a [dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
level plan should represent 10ft in the
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon) and,
like the [campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign)
map, [dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
maps must remain unknown to the players.

Having drawn a cross section and begun mapping of the first few levels,
the referee should give the
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon) a
name and note at least one entrance to the first
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
level on his
[campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign) map.

### Populating a Dungeon

With a dungeon level planned, or substantially so, the referee must
distribute [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2),
[traps](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#tricks-and-traps), and
[treasure](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures) throughout the
maze. The principal
[treasures](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures) should be
placed thoughtfully, then random determination used to fill the balance
of the level.

The referee should throw two six-sided
[dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) for each
unpopulated dungeon location and consult the table of random dungeon
locations.

Delving Deeper Online table2\_3

|                                    |                             |
|------------------------------------|-----------------------------|
| Table 2.3 Random Dungeon Locations |                             |
| 2-12                               | Content                     |
| 2                                  | Treasure guarded by trap    |
| 3                                  | Trick or trap               |
| 4                                  | Treasure guarded by monster |
| 5                                  | Monster                     |
| 6-8                                | Empty room                  |
| 9                                  | Monster                     |
| 10                                 | Treasure guarded by monster |
| 11-12                              | Unguarded treasure          |

#### Empty Rooms

Empty rooms occur frequently and will usually be welcomed even if they
are foreboding or completely nondescript. These might be used by the
players to [rest](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#resting) or
regroup, lay ambushes, establish a defensible position, or whatever else
the referee allows.

#### Monsters

Where Monsters are indicated the referee should consult the random
monster tables for the appropriate
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
level. Note that monsters are not all “meant” to be beatable. Some will
be deadly foes and players should learn to flee from these.
