[Melee](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#melee_2) range is 1" (10
yards) in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration).

#### Monster Reaction

Monster
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
to the players in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
is as per the
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration).

### Evasion and Pursuit

A smaller group may desire to
[evade](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) a
larger group rather than
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
them. Hostile [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2)
(including previously offended
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) residents)
will [pursue](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit)
with a throw of 4-6 on a six-sided die, while non-hostiles will
[pursue](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) only
with a throw of 6.

The possibility of evading an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
is determined by the
[relative](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#relatives) size of the
parties. If the evaders are not more than one-quarter as numerous as the
pursuers they will
[evade](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) with a
throw of 3-6 on a six-sided die. If they are no more than half as
numerous as the pursuers they will
[evade](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) with a
throw of 4-6; otherwise they will
[evade](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) only
with a throw of 5-6.

The odds of
[evasion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) are
adjusted as follows:

#### Surprise

If the pursuers are surprised
[evasion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) is 1
chance in 6 more likely. If the evaders are surprised there is no
opportunity to
[evade](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) unless
low [visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility) or good
[speed](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#speed) dicates otherwise.

#### Low visibility

Woods, misty swamps, night, rain, fog, or snow all increase the chance
of [evasion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) by
1 in 6, even if surprised.

#### Speed

If either side’s [movement
rate](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#movement-rates_1) is at least
twice the other side’s [movement
rate](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#movement-rates_1) the odds of
[evasion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) (or
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit)) are
tipped in their favor by 1 chance in 6, even if surprised.

To resolve a
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit)
scenario the evaders should throw one die. If the result is too low to
[evade](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit), the
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit)
catches up and an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
is unavoidable; otherwise, the evaders have managed to gain ground over
the [pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit).

Assuming the evaders have gained ground, the referee should determine
whether or not the pursuers will continue to give chase. Unless specific
circumstances dictate otherwise, the chase will continue with a throw of
4-6 on a six-sided die. If the pursuers throw high enough they gain
ground and the
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) is
still on; otherwise, they have fallen too far behind and the
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) is
over.

This is repeated until either the pursuers give up or an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
occurs.

Note that mapping is impossible during a
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit). The
referee should position the evaders somewhere within 1-6 hexes of their
starting location at the conclusion of a chase.

Both parties must [rest](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#resting)
for the remainder of the
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) (the day) after
resolving a
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit),
regardless of whether it resulted in an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
or not. At the beginning of the next
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) (day) the players are
considered to be
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost). They will not
know exactly where they are, only that they have endured a long
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) and
covered many leagues in a general direction.

## Seafaring Exploration

As with
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
exploration, ocean regions unknown to the players can be mapped in
advance or as they are explored. The principal features should be placed
thoughtfully with the remainder being filled in by random determination.

The referee can use the random
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
tables to generate ocean regions for seafaring. Hexes of open terrain
should be read as open ocean, woods as coast, mountains as reefs, desert
as islands, and swamp as perpetually stormy ocean. Likewise, rivers
should be read as strong currents,
[fords](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#fords) as confluences of
currents, and trails as navigable seafaring routes. The other features
are as in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
except that villages should be ignored.

### Time and Movement

Seafaring exploration retains the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
exploration timescale of 1
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) per day.

Coastal waters (up to 3 hexes from land) and navigable inland rivers
retain the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
exploration [scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) where
each 1" of [movement
rate](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#movement-rates_1) represents 1
mile traveled per day. The open ocean, however, is so vast and generally
free of obstruction that sailing rate is improved threefold such that 1"
of [movement](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2)
represents 1 league (3 miles) traveled per day.

Exploration by sea is otherwise similar to
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
exploration excepting that players must have an ocean going
[vessel](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels). These are
of two types: [oared](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels)
and sailed.

##### Oared vessels

such as galleys and longships are not restricted by
[wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) direction but
galleys, rafts, and boats are unable to withstand the high seas of the
open ocean. These are limited to coastal waters except in calm
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather).

##### Sailed vessels

such as merchants and warships can run swiftly before the
[wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds), but otherwise
must progress by a series of turns and tacks at impaired
[speed](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#speed). Travel directly into
the [wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) is
generally impossible.

Movement rates for
[oared](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels) ships assume
a full and well trained crew. Poor or incomplete crews can achieve half
the listed rate.

Movement rates for sailing ships assume running fore a fresh
[wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds). All other
[movement](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2) is
at half rate. Note that sailing rates are faster on the open ocean due
to the possibility of sailing unimpeded day and night.

One hexagon should be added when traveling with a current or subtracted
when traveling against a current.

#### Reserves

With the exception of boats and rafts, all sailing ships carry reserve
oars and all [oared](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels)
ships carry reserve
[sails](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#sailed-vessels) to be used
if necessary. These allow
[movement](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2) at
half rate.

#### Resting

All crews require a full day of
[rest](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#resting) after six days at
sea or immediately after weathering a
[storm](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#storms_1).

#### Visibility

Distance to the horizon is determined by height above sea level. From a
ship’s deck [visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility)
is limited to one hex (6 miles). From a crow’s nest a
[sailor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#sailors) can see a ship up
to two hexes (12 miles) away in clear
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather). However,
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) conditions can
severely restrict
[visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility).

### Weather

The [wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds)
[strength](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strength) and direction
should be determined each day at sea. Throw one six-sided die to
determine which hex face the
[wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) is blowing from
and two six-sided [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1)
to determine [wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds)
[strength](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strength).

#### Strong Winds

Boats, rafts, and galleys will capsize in strong
[winds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) on the open
ocean on a throw of 1-2 on a six-sided die each
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns).

#### Storms

Navigation is impossible in storm conditions and any
[vessel](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels) will capsize
on a throw of 1-2 on a six-sided die each
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns). Any
[vessel](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels) that does
not capsize is instead moved 2-7 hexes in a direction secretly
determined by the referee and is immediately considered to be
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost).

### Becoming Lost

A ship’s [captain](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#a-ships-captain)
will have no difficulty navigating a known route so long as the
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) remains fair.
However, should the
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) turn nasty, there
is the possibility of becoming
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost). The referee
should secretly throw a six-sided die for the players each day spent in
strong [winds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds)—a 1-2
indicating they have gotten
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost). If the
players are [lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost)
the referee should
[move](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2) them an
unplanned
[distance](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#encounter-distance_3)/direction
on his map that [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns)
without alerting them.

### Settlements and Strongholds

Settlements and
[strongholds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) occur at
sea as they do in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration).
These can be wholly or partially submerged, built upon floating
pontoons, clinging to rocky prominences, or whatever else the referee
desires. Whether these are friendly or unfriendly can be determined with
a
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
check.

### Encounters at Sea

Wandering [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2)
occur at sea much as they do in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration).
The referee need not check for [wandering
monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wandering-monsters) while
the players are within 3 hexes (18 miles) of a friendly port, but once
out to sea proper he should check once each day on the open ocean or
twice each day along a coast or waterway. An additional check should be
made each day if the players are
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost). A throw of 6
on a six-sided die indicates an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
will occur.

When an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
is indicated, determine the type of
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) by dicing on
the appropriate
[seafaring](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#seafaring-exploration)
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
table. If the players are traveling along a coast or inland waterway an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
is equally likely to occur ashore as at sea. In this case, use the
appropriate
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
table.

#### Surprise

Surprise occurs at sea (as it does in the
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration))
with a throw of 5-6 on a six-sided die. If the players are surprised the
enemy ships or
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) will come at
them from upwind, emerge suddenly out of fog banks or rain squalls,
appear from behind rolling waves, or surface unexpectedly from
underwater.

#### Encounter Distance

If either party is surprised an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
will begin at 10-60 yards distance and the surprised party will be
unable to respond for one
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns); otherwise, an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
will begin at 40-240 yards distance.
[Melee](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#melee_2) range is 1" (10
yards as in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)).
Shipboard artillery range is typically 300 yards.

#### Monster Reaction

Monster
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
to the players at sea is as per the
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration).

### Evasion and Pursuit

Evasion and
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) at
sea is as per the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
with the following additional considerations:

-   Low [visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility)
    occurs in [storms](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#storms_1),
    rain, fog, and at night,
-   Evaders who are able to submerge will automatically escape pursuers
    without this ability unless they are surprised.

### Seafaring Combat

Vessels can engage in ship-to-ship (or ship-to-[sea
monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#sea-monsters))
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat). Ships are treated
much as
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2)—having hull
[dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) instead of [hit
dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice), and
hull points instead of [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).

When ship-to-ship (or ship-to-[sea
monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#sea-monsters))
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) occurs the referee
should use the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat)
[scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) (1" to 10 yards and
one minute [turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns)) to
resolve maneuvering and
[missile](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) fire as the
combatants approach one another.

Wind direction, tactical positions, and
[vessel](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels) facings can
be marked on a [scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) map if
desired or simply noted as closing
[distances](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#encounter-distance_3).
[Oared](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels) ships can
produce a burst of [speed](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#speed)
during [combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat), adding 6"
to [movement rate](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#movement-rates_1)
for up to three [turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) after
which the crew is exhausted.

#### Missile Fire

Ship-board artillery may be fired every other
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) while
[spells](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#explanation-of-spells) and
[missiles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) may be
loosed each [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns). [Normal
missiles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#normal-missiles) are
ineffective against ship hulls but are allowed their maximum outdoor
range, giving due consideration to
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) conditions and
ocean swell.

Small galleys are assumed to carry a single artillery battery on the
fore deck. Large galleys carry two batteries (one fore and one aft), and
warships carry four batteries (one each fore, aft, port, and starboard).
Artillery hits cause 2-12 hull points of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) and will hole a
ship below the waterline on any score of 10 or more hull points. A holed
ship will sink in 3-18
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat)
[turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) (minutes) unless
repairs are made.

#### Ramming

Medieval ships are not generally built for ramming but a faster ship may
ram a slower ship in the side, circumstances permitting. The ramming
ship sustains one hull die
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) while the rammed
ship sustains half the rammer’s hull
[dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) (rounded down) in
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage). If 10 or more hull
points are sustained the ship is holed below the waterline and will sink
in 3-18 [turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns). Meanwhile,
boarding may ensue.

#### Melee

When ships [ram](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#ramming), grapple,
or come along side for boarding the referee is advised to use the
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat)
[scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) (1" to 10ft and one
minute [turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns)) to resolve
any hand-to-hand [combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat).
Ship deck plans can be used much as
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon) maps
for this purpose. Troops fleeing from
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) will only pitch
themselves overboard in fair
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) near to land;
otherwise they will surrender.

### Swimming

Any player character who grew up on the coast or by a watercourse can
swim, as can any non-player character who throws a 4-6 on a six-sided
die. Swimming is at a rate of 6" in ideal circumstances; otherwise 3". A
character can swim for at most a single day after which he will
[drown](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#drowning).

### Drowning

Anyone pitched into the sea risks drowning. Half of any ship’s crew
cannot [swim](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#swimming) and will
automatically drown; otherwise, unarmored
[men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) who can
[swim](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#swimming) will survive with a
throw of 2-6 on a six-sided die if they immediately rid themselves of
anything heavier than a
[dagger](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#daggers). Each heavier item
retained increases the risk of drowning by 1 in 6. Leather and mail
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) count for
one and four items, respectively, and plate
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) causes
automatic drowning. During a
[storm](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#storms_1) there is always a
minimum of 3 chances in 6 of drowning. Survival indicates that the
character has managed to remove his
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) before
drowning.

## Aerial Exploration

Should the players acquire winged mounts they can map
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
and ocean regions by aerial exploration.

The referee may also wish to include cloud top regions which can only be
reached on the wing. The referee can use the random
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
tables to generate cloud top regions for aerial exploration. Hexes of
open terrain should be read as vacant air, woods as islands of solid
cloud, mountains as cloud piercing or floating peaks, desert as
dangerously insubstantial islands of cloud, and swamp as perpetually
stormy regions. Likewise, rivers should represent persistent currents,
[fords](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#fords) should represent
confluences of currents, and trails should represent navigable tunnels
or air ways. The other features are as per the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
except that villages should be ignored.

### Time and Movement

Aerial exploration retains the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
exploration timescale of 1
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) per day.

There are two modes of travel on the wing: low and high altitude.

At low altitude it is possible to observe or remain in contact with
ground-level activity including
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) and
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat). However, at low
altitude fliers must allow for hazards and turbulence and must weave
routes around, between, or over terrain features.

At high altitude progress is unimpeded other than by the need to roost
overnight; [movement
rate](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#movement-rates_1) is generally
double that achieved at low altitude.

#### Visibility

Distance to the horizon is
[relative](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#relatives) to altitude.
In clear [weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather)
[visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility) is 2-6
hexagons (up to 36 miles) from low altitude, or 11-16 hexes (up to 100
miles) from a lofty mountain summit. However, poor
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) conditions and
intervening mountains will severely restrict
[visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility). From a
high altitude
[visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility) is 11-16
hexes (up to 100 miles) in perfect
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather), but is usually
limited by cloud cover.

#### Resting

Flying creatures other than [air
elementals](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elementals-air) need to
roost overnight (or during the day if they travel at night).
Additionally, flying creatures other than
[dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) and [air
elementals](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elementals-air) require
a full day of [rest](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#resting) after
six days on the
[move](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2). [Air
elementals](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elementals-air) are
tireless fliers, while
[dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) require a full
week of sleep after six weeks of activity.

### Weather

Although travel by air is quick it is severely affected by poor
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather).

Weather conditions should be determined by the referee for each day of
[aerial](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#aerial-exploration)
exploration. Throw one six-sided die to determine which hex face the
[wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) is blowing from
and two [dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) to
determine [wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds)
[strength](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strength).
[Aerial](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#aerial-exploration) travel
can be dangerous in strong
[winds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) and
[storms](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#storms_1); travelers risk
being dashed into obstacles, struck by lightning or flying debris, and
so on.

##### Strong Winds

Normal-type flying creatures, [flying
carpets](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#flying-carpet), [flying
broomsticks](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#flying-broomstick), and
the like will crash in strong
[winds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) with a throw
of 1-2 on a six-sided die, checked once each
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns).

##### Storms

Navigation is impossible in storm conditions and any flying creatures
(other than [air
elementals](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elementals-air)) or
[vessels](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels) will crash
with a throw of 1-2 on a six-sided die. A flier that does not crash is
instead moved 2-7 hexes in a direction secretly determined by the
referee and is immediately considered to be
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost).

### Becoming Lost

A flier will have no difficulty navigating a known route so long as the
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) remains fair.
However, should the
[weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) turn nasty, it is
possible to become
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost). The referee
should secretly throw a six-sided die for the players each day spent in
strong [winds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds)—a 1-2
indicating that they have gotten
[lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost). If the
players are [lost](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#becoming-lost)
the referee should
[move](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2) them an
unplanned
[distance](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#encounter-distance_3)/direction
on his map that [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns)
without alerting them.

### Settlements and Strongholds

Settlements and
[strongholds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) occur in
the air as they do in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration).
At low altitude these are likely to be on the ground. If these are
discovered at high altitude they could be levitating towers, built upon
cloud banks, suspended by squadrons of hot air balloons, or whatever
else the referee desires. Whether these will be friendly or unfriendly
can be determined with a
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
check.

### Aerial Encounters

Encounters occur in the air much as they do in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration).
The referee should check once each day with a throw of a 6 on a
six-sided die indicating an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters).

When an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
occurs determine the type of
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) by dicing on
the appropriate
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
table. If the players are traveling at low altitude the
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
is equally likely to occur on the surface as on the wing. In this case
use the appropriate
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
table.

#### Surprise

Surprise occurs in the air (as it does in the
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration))
with a throw of 5-6 on a six-sided die. If the players are surprised
their enemies will typically come at them from upwind or above, emerge
suddenly out of clouds or rain squalls, or emerge from the dazzling
glare of the sun.

#### Encounter Distance

If either party is surprised an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
will begin at 10-60 yards distance and the surprised party will be
unable to respond for one
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns); otherwise, an
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
will begin at 40-240 yards distance.
[Melee](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#melee_2) range is 1" (10
yards) as it is in the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration).
Airborne artillery range is typically 300 yards.

#### Monster Reaction

Monster
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
to the players on the wing is as per the
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration).

### Evasion and Pursuit

Evasion and
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) on
the wing is as per the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
with the following additional considerations:

-   Low [visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility)
    occurs in [storms](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#storms_1),
    rain, clouds, looking into the sun, and at night,
-   Evaders who can [fly](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#fly) will
    automatically escape pursuers on the ground without this ability
    unless they are surprised.

### Aerial Combat

Players with winged mounts or other means of flight can engage in
[aerial](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#aerial-exploration)
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat). Excepting [air
elementals](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elementals-air), larger
creatures are clumsier fliers than are smaller creatures. Climbing is
slow and diving is fast.

When air-to-air [combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat)
occurs, the referee should use the
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat)
[scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) (1" to 10 yards and
one minute [turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns)) to
resolve maneuvering and
[missile](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) fire as the
protagonists engage. Altitude,
[wind](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strong-winds) direction,
tactical positions, and facings can be marked on a
[scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) map, if desired, or
simply noted as closing
[distances](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#encounter-distance_3).

#### Missile Fire

Airborne artillery may be fired every other
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns), while
[spells](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#explanation-of-spells) and
[missiles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) may be
loosed each [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) giving due
consideration to air [speed](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#speed)
and [weather](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#weather) conditions.

Large creatures can bombard ground targets by dropping rocks, logs,
bodies, or similar
[missiles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) from above.
These are treated as artillery attacks.

Missile fire from the air is always considered to be at long range and,
against [aerial](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#aerial-exploration)
targets, attack rolls are penalized by −4.

A [mounted](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#mounted-combat)
[heroic-type](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#heroic-types) is
subject to [missile](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire)
fire only on a six-sided die throw of 5-6; otherwise his mount is
subject to that
[missile](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) fire. Should
a rider be hit he is unhorsed with a throw of 6 on a six-sided die and
will [fall](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#falling). Otherwise, a
hit to his mount will maim a critical flight muscle with a throw of 6 on
a six-sided die and cause it to crash to the ground.

#### Melee

Aerial melee attacks are made in passing clashes at a range of 1" (10
yards) with combatants being disengaged after each pass. Should a
combatant lose the
[initiative](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#initiative) he is
unable to riposte that [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns)
unless his [speed](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#speed) and
heading match his opponent’s, or the combatants are otherwise held
together.

### Falling

Falling or otherwise crashing is a constant hazard for fliers. A fall to
earth from a low altitude will cause 1-6
[dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) (1-6 to 6-36 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice)). A
fall to earth from a high altitude will cause 10-60 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) after 1-4
[turns](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) (minutes) free
falling.

## The Campaign

#### Specialist Hirelings

Specialists are the elite category of
[hirelings](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hirelings) whose
services are only available to the wealthy. Specialists are engaged to
undertake specific tasks and must be paid for a minimum of one month.

##### Alchemists

can duplicate [potions](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#potions)
from a sample or a proven formula at one-half the
[potion’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#potions) regular cost.
They can also
[research](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#researching-new-spells)
new [potions](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#potions) (including
[poisons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#neutralize-poison)
although use of
[poison](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#neutralize-poison) is an
evil act) at double the cost of a
[magic-user’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-magic-user)
equivalent spell
[research](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#researching-new-spells).

##### Animal Trainers

are necessary to train any non-domesticated creatures. An animal trainer
can train one specific type of creature and no more than six such
creatures can be trained at any one time. The duration of any training
will be determined by the referee.

##### At least one Armorer

is required to maintain the arms and
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) of every
50 [fighters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-fighter). While
otherwise idle an armorer can fashion up to three
[shields](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) or two
[helms](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#magical-helms) per week, one
suit of mail
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) in a
month, or one suit of plate
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) in two
months. Two assistant
[smiths](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#at-least-one-smith) will
double this volume. Six assistant
[smiths](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#at-least-one-smith) will
triple this volume.

##### Assassins

can be found only rarely; no more than 1-6 are available in any game
year. Success is determined by the referee according to the power and
precautions taken by the subject. Hiring an assassin is considered an
evil act.

##### An Engineer

is required for the construction of any bridge,
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds), or other
fortification. They are also required to undermine fortified walls and
for any tunneling or mining.

##### Marines

are sea-faring fighters. In ship-to-ship
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) they are equivalent
to [mercenaries](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men-mercenaries);
they wear only leather
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) and are
never [mounted](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#mounted-combat).

##### A Sage

is a master of esoteric knowledge who can function in an advisory
capacity.

##### Sailors

are required to [man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) any
sea-faring ship. In ship-to-ship
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) they are equivalent
to [buccaneers](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men-buccaneers).

##### A Ship’s Captain

is required to effectively run any sea-faring
[vessel](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels), maintaining
order, discipline, and sea worthiness.

##### At least one Smith

is required to maintain horseshoes, harness, buckles, axles, wheels, and
so on for every 50 [horses](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#horses).
While otherwise idle a smith can fashion one score
[arrow](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#arrows-and-bolts) heads,
four [spears](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#spears), two
[axes](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#axes) or swords, or a single
two-handed sword per week.

##### Spies

can be found only rarely; no more than 1-6 are available in any game
year. These are used to infiltrate, eavesdrop,
[shadow](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#shadows), and spy for the
obtaining or planting of information or trinkets. Success is determined
by the referee according to the precautions taken by the subject.

### Constructing a Stronghold

A wealthy character may wish to construct a
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) such as a
[keep](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#keep), tower, castle, or
whatever is affordable. If he has reached 9th level he is always allowed
to establish this
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds);
otherwise, he will require permission from the regional ruler. Depending
upon the character’s
[alignment](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#alignment),
[charisma](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#charisma), and political
prospects, such permission may not always be forthcoming.

Monsters must be cleared from within three hexes (18 miles) of the site
before any construction can commence. Once a fortification has been
established, however, the surrounds will remain clear of
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) so long as
they are patrolled satisfactorily.

The region within three hexes of a
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) (37 hexes
total) will typically contain 2-8 villages of 100-400 inhabitants; these
and other features can be determined by the referee using the random
[wilderness](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-exploration)
hex tables. If the occupier of a
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) is at
least 9th level he is entitled to collect 1 gp per month from each
inhabitant for their protection.
[Clerics](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-cleric) may collect an
additional 1 gp per month for spiritual donations where alms are
provided and services conducted.

These revenues may be used by the player to swell his personal treasury
or to further his fledgling realm with roads, bridges, fortifications,
inns, churches, animal husbandry, or whatever else. How these activities
will influence the character’s reputation and his political prospects is
for the referee to decide.

Below are the costs of common structures though any variation in size
should adjust costs proportionately.

##### Arrow Slit

Any fortified opening through which
[missiles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#missile-fire) can be
discharged including murder holes and oilettes.

##### Barbette

A 10ft diameter, 20ft tall [round
tower](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#tower-round) section which
protrudes where battlement walls intersect, enabling archers to fire
through [arrow slits](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#arrow-slit).

##### Barbican

A pair of 30ft diameter, 40ft tall crenulated towers with a 40ft section
of [curtain wall](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#curtain-wall)
between them having battlements facing both inward and outward. The wall
may be serviced by a gate with
[portcullis](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#portcullis) and
[drawbridge](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#drawbridge) (at
additional cost).

##### Bastion

A 125ft section of [curtain
wall](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#curtain-wall) curved in an
80ft diameter semi-circle.

##### Battering Ram

A heavy log [ram](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#ramming) suspended
beneath a carriage on wheels or carried with handles. Used to batter
down gates by force.

##### Building

A 40ft wide and 20ft deep, two-story structure with both attic and
basement. The wooden and stone versions are of identical design.

##### Catapult, Heavy

A mighty siege engine that lobs rocks up to 480 yards for 3-18 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage), firing every third
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) with a complete crew.

##### Catapult, Light

A siege engine that lobs rocks up to 300 yards for 2-12 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage), firing every
second [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) with a complete
crew.

##### Cauldron

A timber frame that suspends a great cauldron over the battlements,
enabling defenders to pour boiling water or oil over the walls.

##### Curtain Wall

A 100ft long section of 15ft high crenulated castle wall.

##### Ditch

A 100ft long section of 10ft deep and 20ft wide diggings. Fills with
water in wet environments, forming a moat. Costs half if a
[rampart](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#rampart) is also
constructed.

##### Door, Iron

A great [door](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#doors) constructed of
iron. A double-width gate costs triple.

##### Door, Reinforced

A heavy hardwood [door](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#doors)
reinforced with tempered iron bands. A double-width gate costs triple.

##### Door, Wooden

A stout hardwood [door](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#doors). A
double-width gate costs triple.

##### Drawbridge

A wooden bridge up to 20ft long and 10ft wide affixed to a gate that is
used to cross a [ditch](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#ditch).
Includes a winch used to raise or lower the bridge.

##### Gatehouse

A 30ft long by 20ft wide fortification with 20ft high crenulated walls.
Includes a double-width iron gate,
[portcullis](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#portcullis) and
[drawbridge](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#drawbridge).

##### Keep

A 250ft long section of [curtain
wall](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#curtain-wall) arranged in an
80ft diameter circle with an integrated
[gatehouse](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#gatehouse) all
surrounding a 40ft diameter, 60ft high crenulated circular tower.

##### Palisade

A 100ft long section of 8ft high timber pickets. Usually a temporary or
cheap structure in lieu of stonework defenses.

##### Portcullis

A heavy iron grate up to 12ft high and 8ft wide that can be raised and
lowered to protect a gateway.

##### Rampart

A 100ft long, 20ft wide and 10ft high pile of earth used for shelter or
concealment or to raise the ground level outside a wall in order to
surmount it. Costs half if a
[ditch](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#ditch) is also constructed.

##### Siege Tower

A 15ft tall wooden structure on wheels used to assail
[stronghold](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strongholds) walls.

##### Stairs, Stone

Up to a 10ft rise or fall of internal or external stone steps.

##### Stairs, Wooden

Up to a 10ft rise or fall of internal or external wooden steps.

##### Tower, Round

Up to 20ft diameter, 30ft tall round tower with crenulated battlements.

##### Tower, Small

Up to 15ft diameter, 40ft tall [round
tower](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#tower-round) with crenulated
battlements.

##### Tower, Square

Up to 30ft square, 30ft high tower with crenulated battlements.

##### Window

A glass covered frame for admitting
[light](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#light_2), up to 3ft square.
Can be opened for better
[visibility](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#visibility).

### Mass Battles

Strongholds may need to defend themselves or the surrounding territory
from hostile or ambitious neighbors. Political intrigues, sieges, and
field battles are all possible. While the
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) rules herein can
resolve actions involving large bodies of troops, the referee may desire
to employ purpose-made wargaming rules for
full-[scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) fantasy battles.
Suitable rules for these engagements include “Chainmail” (1971), “De
Bellis Fantasticus—Here There Be
[Dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons)” (1998), and “The
Book of War” (2011).

### Artifacts

Super powerful magic items aligned toward law, neutrality, or chaos
might exist at the referee’s option. These potentially game-altering
objects are known as artifacts and should be handled by the referee with
great care.

Artifacts are unique,
[campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign) specific
objects that have a
[purpose](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#purpose) and a history. An
artifact could be a throne, an extra-dimensional gate, a crown, a suit
of mechanized
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields), an
enchanted ship, a sword of seven shards, or anything else the referee
desires. They will be the subject of
[research](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#researching-new-spells)
and controversy among the wisest and may also be known through folklore
to the common [man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men).

Whatever its nature, an artifact is impervious to ordinary magic.
[Anti-magic
shield](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#anti-magic-shield), [remove
curse](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#remove-curse), [dispel
magic](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dispel-magic), [dispel
evil](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dispel-evil), and so on are
completely ineffective. Moreover, an artifact is almost completely
indestructible. There is typically only one specific way to destroy an
artifact which invariably involves a great
[quest](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#quest) to some faraway and
dangerous place.

Consequences for meddling with an artifact of differing
[alignment](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#alignment) should be
severe. Death, insanity, extra-dimensional imprisonment, 10-60 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage), loss of 1-6
experience levels, or similar would not be unreasonable. The power
imbued when employing an artifact appropriately should be equally
astonishing and this matter is left entirely to the referee’s
imagination...

### Enchanting Magic Items

Magic-users and
[clerics](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-cleric) can copy
[spells](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#explanation-of-spells)
which they can memorize onto
[scrolls](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#spellbooks-and-scrolls)
and can enchant other magical items at 9th level or higher. Items with
spell-like powers that mimic
[magic-user](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-magic-user) or
[cleric](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-cleric)
[spells](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#explanation-of-spells) can
only be constructed by members of that
[class](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#classes); other magic items
can be created by either
[class](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#classes).

The referee can extrapolate cost and time requirements for other items
commensurate with their power and value. Invest wisely.

### Other Worlds

There are countless other
[worlds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#creating-a-world) to
explore that might be reached by magic or by other ingenuity. Moreover,
the inhabitants of these unfathomable places might reach the here and
now of the [campaign](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-campaign)
at any time, or may have been present from the very beginning.

Visiting other planets, other times, or other dimensions are very real
possibilities and the players might discover paths to abyssal depths,
Elysian delights, or virtually any other place at any time. The
possibilities are truly endless.

Should the players reach other
[worlds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#creating-a-world) these
should be remarkably different from our own. The assumed natural laws of
gravity, time,
[space](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#space-required),
temperature, inflammability,
[scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale), and so on should not
all apply. In this regard the wealth of science fiction and fantasy
literature can be a great inspiration to the referee.

# Section III: Monsters & Treasures

## Monsters

Monsters are the principal challenge that players will face in their
adventures. They include all the genuine horrors of the
[underworld](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#underworld-exploration)
such as [trolls](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#trolls),
[vampires](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#vampires), and
[dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons), as well as all
the non-player characters of the
[world](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#creating-a-world). Every
character that is not run by a player is a monster—even the good
townsfolk and the players’
[hirelings](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hirelings).

It is clear then that not all monsters are harmful to the players. Some
are quite benign and may even be helpful. Others are completely
disinterested in the players so long as they don’t get in the way, while
yet others are villainous threats that will seek to slay, capture, or
waylay the players. A monster’s initial disposition toward the players
is determined by a
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
check and its
[alignment](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#alignment). This
characteristic is a one word summary of any monster’s stance in the
eternal struggle between law, chaos, and neutrality.

### Summary of Monsters

##### Number Appearing and Number in

Lair are the numbers of
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) typically
encountered outside of or in their lair, respectively. A + indicates the
possibility of leader-types and/or accompanying
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2). The number
of [monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) appearing
outside the lair is appropriate for 4-6 characters whose experience
level is equal to the
[monster’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) number of
[hit dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).
The referee can [scale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#scale) these
figures for smaller or larger groups or as desired.

##### AC

is for [armor class](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#melee).

##### Movement Rates

are given in inches per
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns). The first figure
denotes the normal ground rate. If a secondary rate appears it denotes
the flying, [swimming](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#swimming),
burrowing, or climbing rate as per the
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) description.

##### HD

lists the number of [hit
dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) with
any adjustment to [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice)
being applied after the given number of six-sided
[dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-dice_1) have been thrown
and summed.

##### Lair Nearby

is the percentage chance that any encountered
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) will be from
a nearby lair. “Nearby” is
[relative](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#relatives) to the
[monster’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) usual mode
of locomotion. Whether the lair is easy or difficult to locate is for
the referee to determine.

##### Treasure Type

is for determining what
[treasure](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures) will be
present in the lair. A \* indicates the possibility of additional
[treasure](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures) as per the
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) description.

##### Alignment

L is for lawful, N is for neutral, and C is for chaotic. Some
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) can be of any
[alignment](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#alignment)
([men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) being among these) and
others can be either of two
[alignments](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#alignment)
([elves](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#elves_1) and
[kobolds](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#kobolds) being among
these). In all these cases any individual is always of exactly one
[alignment](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#alignment).

## Explanation of Monsters

Wherever special melee
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) is detailed it is
applicable to [heroic](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#heroic-types)
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) only. However,
against
[normal-types](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#normal-types),
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) throw one
attack roll as a 1 [hit
die](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hit-dice)
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) for each of
their own [hit die](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hit-dice), with
each successful attack roll causing 1-6 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage).

Monster [saving
throws](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#saving-throws) are as the
most appropriate player-type with as many experience levels as the
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) has [hit
dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice). For
example, an [android](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#androids)
would save as a 2nd level
[magic-user](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-magic-user), a
[troll](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#trolls) would save as a 6th
level [fighter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-fighter), and so
on. A [gothrog](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#gothrogs) would save
as a 10th level
[fighter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-fighter)/10th level
[magic-user](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-magic-user), using
whichever category is more favorable.

##### Androids

are artificial [men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men). They
often have superior qualities such as health, grace, comeliness, or
education, but are otherwise indistinguishable save for the color of
their blood. Some individuals possess mind powers equivalent to magic
use of up to the 4th experience level (throw a six-sided die and
subtract 2 for each android—a result less than 1 indicating no tangible
mind powers); otherwise, they function as do ordinary
[men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men).

##### Ants, Giant

are 2-3ft long. They are industrious tunnelers and gatherers that occur
in great colonies. Outside the lair only the soldier types will be
encountered. Within the lair two-thirds of any ants encountered are 1
[hit die](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#hit-dice) workers that
will not attack unless provoked. The remainder are soldiers that will
attack anything that obstructs the business of the colony. A nest always
has a 10 [hit
dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) queen
ant who is immobile and non-aggressive.
[Giant](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#giants) ants will never flee
from their nest unless the queen is slain.

##### Apes

are generally non-aggressive but are extremely strong. They will climb
trees for refuge but if provoked they can strike for 2-7 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage).

##### Basilisks

are large, slow, eight-legged reptiles whose gaze or touch will petrify
any living creature that fails to save [versus
petrification](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#paralysis-and-petrification).
If it is tricked into seeing its own reflection in a mirror, a basilisk
will likewise be petrified.

##### Bats

roost underground in great numbers during the day. They are mostly
harmless to [man-types](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#man-types)
but if a colony is startled and takes to the wing in a confined
[space](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#space-required) they will
create confusion. A flapping cloud of
[bats](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#bats-giant) will obscure
sight and possibly extinguish torches, cause
[equipment](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#equipment) to be
dropped, or cause spell
[casting](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#spell-casting-from-memory)
to be interrupted.

##### Bats, Giant

are black as night and so silent on the wing that they will
[surprise](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#surprise) their prey with
a throw of 3 or more on a six-sided die. If their prey resists they will
shriek, causing
[normal-types](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#normal-types) to
cover their ears for one
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) rather than fight.

##### Bears

are omnivorous but favor meat. They have rather poor eyesight but an
excellent sense of smell and can scent food from miles away. They can be
aggressive hunters and are very powerful. They cause 3-8 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) or, if an attack
roll exceeds the number required to hit by 4 or more or is a 20 in any
case, 4-14 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage).

##### Beetles, Giant

are of various sorts but are invariably hungry and can eat virtually any
organic matter. They occur underground and in forests and can tunnel
through soft earth. They do not hear or see well and rely on their
sensitivity to vibrations and smell.

##### A Black Pudding

is an amorphous black blob which
[moves](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2) about a
[dungeon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#populating-a-dungeon)
scavenging the leavings of other inhabitants. Due to its coloration and
shapelessness it is very difficult to spot in dim
[light](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#light_2) or shadows. It is
susceptible to fire but invulnerable to cold. Lightning and slashing
attacks will divide it into smaller parts without causing harm. Contact
with a black pudding will dissolve wood and metal
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) in one
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns). Flesh is likewise
dissolved suffering 3-18 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) per
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns). Stone, however, is
impervious. It can
[move](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2) along
walls, floors, and ceilings without difficulty and can squeeze through
tiny openings including cracks in stonework and under
[doors](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#doors).

##### Boars

are wild pigs that occur in forests and on plains. They are frequently
hunted for sport but are extremely tough; they always make one more
attack roll after being reduced to 0 or fewer [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).
Every other boar encountered will be a sounder and if these young are
attacked the adults will always attack and will absolutely not flee.

##### Boars, Giant

are similar to regular
[boars](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#boars) but for their great
size and aggressive demeanor. They will attack anyone who enters their
territory causing 2-12 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage). They will never
retreat and will always make one more attack roll after being reduced to
0 or fewer [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).

##### Cave Bears

are enormous carnivorous
[bears](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#bears) that are always
hungry. They have rather poor eyesight but an excellent sense of smell
and can scent food from miles away. They are aggressive hunters and are
extremely powerful. They cause 1-11 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) or, if an attack
roll exceeds the number required to hit by 4 or more or is a 20 in any
case, 3-18 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage). Cave bears will
always make one more attack roll after being reduced to 0 or fewer [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).

##### Cavemen

are large but primitive Neanderthal types who are otherwise similar to
[men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men). They fight with crude
[axes](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#axes), hammers, and clubs,
but suffer a −1 adjustment to
[morale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
checks and have little
[treasure](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures). Leader-types
are always [fighters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-fighter)
but never possess magic items.

##### Centaurs

are
[horse](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#horses)-[men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)
having the body of a [horse](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#horses)
and the torso of a human. They have normal human
[intelligence](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#intelligence) and
dwell in secluded glens and valleys in deep forests. Centaurs equip
themselves with [spears](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#spears)
(25%), swords (25%), or clubs (50%) and
[shields](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) with
half carrying short [bows](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#bows) in
addition. Moreover, a centaur warrior can has two attack rolls each
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns), once each with his
weaponry and hooves. A centaur lair is much as a small human village
having two mares and two foals for every warrior stallion present. Mares
have one attack roll each
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) only under duress and
foals are non-combative.

##### Centipedes, Giant and Large

are found almost anywhere and are aggressive hunters. Large specimens
are up to 1ft long, while the
[giant](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#giants) types are up to 10ft
long and have a hard, armored head but a relatively soft body. Both
sorts [move](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#time-and-movement_2)
along walls and ceilings at normal
[speed](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#speed). The bite of either
causes paralysis although a [saving
throw](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#saving-throws) is allowed and
is at +4 in the case of large centipedes.

##### Chimeras

are fearsome three-headed
[monsters](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) with great
[bat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#bats-giant)-like wings, the
forequarters of a [lion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#lions), the
hindquarters of a goat, and the heads of goat,
[lion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#lions), and
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons). A chimera can use
its [breath weapon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#breath-weapon)
or engage in [combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat). The
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) head breathes a 6"
long 2" wide cone of fire that deals 3-18 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage), although a
successful [saving
throw](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#saving-throws) [versus breath
weapons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#breath-weapon) will reduce
this by half. In [combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) a
chimera has three attack rolls each
[turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) against
[heroic](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#heroic-types) enemies; the
goat head butting or goring, the
[lion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#lions) head biting or rending
with its paws, and the
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) head biting.

##### Cockatrices

are reptilian-fowl with
[bat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#bats-giant)-like wings. The
merest touch of its tail feathers will petrify any living thing (other
than a cockatrice) that fails to save [versus
petrification](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#paralysis-and-petrification).

##### Crabs, Giant

occur underwater, in coastal estuaries, and in swamps. They have hard,
armored shells and if an attack roll exceeds the number required to hit
by 4 or more, or is a 20 in any case, they cause 1-11 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice)
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage).

##### Crocodiles

are voracious reptiles found in rivers and swamps of warm regions. They
are difficult to spot when floating half-submerged in water and will
often attack by
[surprise](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#surprise). If an attack
roll exceeds the number required to hit by 4 or more a crocodile will
drag its victim back into the water where it will roll over and over
until the victim is drowned. Crocodiles are lazy and will not
[pursue](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) more
than one [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) out of water.

##### Crocodiles, Giant

are thrice the size of their ordinary cousins but otherwise similar. An
attack causes 2-12 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) and any attack roll
that exceeds the number required to hit by 4 or more swallows a
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-sized victim whole. They
are difficult to spot as they float half-submerged in water and they can
overturn boats and rafts. A
[giant](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#giants)
[crocodile](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#crocodiles) can be
rammed by larger ships, possibly slaying the
[monster](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#monsters_2) but also
capsizing the boat (check separately for each).

##### Cyborgs

were once [men](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) but are now
mostly machines; inhumane and evil. They can occur in large numbers and
aim to sweep across a population assimilating all
[man-types](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#man-types) into cyborgs.
They are cruelly strong and deal 3-8 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) on a hit, need
never check
[morale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks),
and will never give up a
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) so
long as the quarry is in sight.

##### Cyclopes

are 20ft tall [giants](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#giants) with
but one large eye which is the cause of poor depth perception and a −2
adjustment on all attack rolls. They dwell in forlorn, out of the way
ruins, islands, or undersea caves where they seldom
[encounter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#wilderness-encounters)
others. They are skilled
[smiths](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#at-least-one-smith) and
should a player offer a useful gift and get a positive
[reaction](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
the cyclopes may offer magical
[armor](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields) in
return. A cyclops does battle with a huge club and deals 6-21 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) and can hurl rocks
up to 20" for 2-12 [damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage).
They especially prize gold and their
[treasure](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures) hoard will
always contain an additional 2,000-5,000 gp.

### Dinosaurs

Dinosaurs are great, prehistoric
[lizards](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#lizards-giant-and-large)
and can be fearsome enemies. The largest predators are few but can
swallow [man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-sized victims
whole while the smaller types occur in hunting packs. Herbivores of all
sizes appear in herds. None of them covets
[treasure](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#treasures).

##### Dinosaurs, Brontosaurs

are among the largest creatures walking on land. They are up to 80ft
long, 20ft tall at the shoulder, and can weigh over 30 tons. They spend
their time grazing the vegetation of the great plains and swamplands.
Fortunately, they are peaceful herbivores and unlikely to attack unless
provoked. The chief danger they present is from crushing, barging, or
stampeding ahead of predators or fire. Hits deal 3-18 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) due to their
immense mass.

##### Dinosaurs, Deinonychus

include any of the relatively small pack hunting carnivores up to 5ft
high and 10ft long. They are quick and cunning and inclined to stalk
prey, only attacking at the optimal moment. They will not give up a
[pursuit](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#evasion-and-pursuit) while
their prey remains in sight.

##### Dinosaurs, Mosasaurs

are huge reptilian swimmers up to 40ft in length. These
[marine](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#marines)
[lizards](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#lizards-giant-and-large)
have paddle-like limbs, finned tails, and huge jaws bristling with
curved teeth. They are found in any deep waters but must surface to
breathe air. A hit causes 3-18 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) but if ever an
attack roll exceeds the number required to hit by 4 or more, or is a 20
in any case, a mosasaur will swallow a
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-sized target whole.

##### Dinosaurs, Pterodactyls

are any [man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-sized and larger
reptilian fliers that rule the prehistoric skies. They occur in coastal
and swampy regions where they nest in colonies that cling to cliff
faces, cave walls, and escarpments, and are always hungry. The most
common forms are approximately
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-sized with wingspans of
10-25ft but the largest sorts are up to 20ft tall with wingspans of up
to 40ft.

##### Dinosaurs, Stegosaurs

are large herbivores up to 30ft long and 10ft high and up to 3 tons in
weight. These have very tiny brains and a distinctive array of
[shield](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#armor-and-shields)-like
plates along the ridge of the spine, granting AC 2 versus attacks other
than from the flank. They have a fist of 2ft long spikes on the tail
which will strike for 2-12 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) to the flank or
rear; otherwise, [damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) is
3-8 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).

##### Dinosaurs, Triceratops

are huge, aggressive herbivores that will run down any threat to the
herd. They are up to 30ft long and 10ft high and can weigh up to 10
tons. A triceratops has a huge skull with a distinctive bony frill and
three great horns granting AC 2 from the front. Should it charge an
enemy it will deal 4-24 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage); otherwise,
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) is 2-12 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice).

##### Dinosaurs, Tyrannosaurus Rexes

are huge carnivorous
[lizards](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#lizards-giant-and-large)
and truly fearsome predators. They are up to 20ft tall and 40ft long and
can weigh up to 7 tons. The jaws contain scores of
[dagger](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#daggers)-like fangs and any
hit causes 4-24 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage). On any attack roll
that exceeds the number required to hit by 4 or more, or is a 20 in any
case, it will swallow a
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-sized target whole.

##### A Djinni

is a creature of air appearing as a supremely confident, bare-chested
warrior. They can [fly](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#fly) as
easily as walk, even burdened with thrice what an ordinary
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men) could bear. A djinni can
become invisible, assume [gaseous
form](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#gaseous-form), or magically
create any desired object at will. Soft materials including food, drink,
and garments are permanent. Harder materials have a shorter existence;
djinn gold lasts only a day, steel only an hour. A djinni can also
create magical
[illusions](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#illusions) on a whim and
these are equal to the
[phantasm](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#phantasm) spell except
that a djinni has no need to concentrate to maintain the
[illusion](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#illusions).

A djinni can also transform into a torrid whirlwind 3" high and 2" wide
which will sweep away all
[normal-types](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#normal-types). The
whirlwind takes one [turn](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#turns) to
form and another to dissipate. A djinni deals 1-11 [hit
points](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice) of
[damage](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#damage) in
[combat](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#combat) due to his
formidable size and
[strength](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#strength).

##### Dogs

are keen nosed pack animals that inhabit plains and prairies. They can
be trained only if separated from the pack as pups but will then have +2
[loyalty](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#retainer-loyalty).

##### Doppelgangers

are humanoid creatures that can change their physical form to
identically resemble any
[man](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#men)-like creature they have
observed. Once a likeness is achieved they can do away with the victim
and then act in his role for a time to gain the utmost advantage before
attacking again. Doppelgangers are immune to
[sleep](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#sleep) and charm spells and
make [saving throws](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#saving-throws)
as a 10th level
[fighter](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-fighter).

##### Dragon Turtles

are 30ft diameter turtles with long, sinuous necks and
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) heads. They are
found only in large bodies of water and lair in deep, underwater
grottos.

A [dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) turtle has a
9"×3" conical [breath
weapon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#breath-weapon) of scalding
steam which functions as does a
[dragon’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) [breath
weapon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#breath-weapon). It can
surface beneath even a large ship, having a 50% chance of capsizing the
[vessel](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#oared-vessels).

### Dragons

Dragons are the great flying wyrms of
[legend](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#legend-and-rumors) and are
always
[heroic](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#heroic-types)/[superheroic](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#superheroic-types),
regardless of [hit
dice](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#the-numbers-of-hit-dice). They
are of six types: white, black, green, blue, red, and golden and have
the following characteristics:

White [dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) are the
least intelligent sort and have the usual 20% chance of knowing the
common tongue and no possibility of magic use. [Golden
dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons-golden) are the
most intelligent sort and they always know the common tongue and always
have the use of magic
[spells](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#explanation-of-spells). The
other [dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) have
various chances of speaking the common tongue and only 10% chance of
being magic-using.

All [dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) have six life
stages: hatchling, young, adult, mature, old, and ancient. The size of a
[dragon’s](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) [breath
weapon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#breath-weapon) is determined
according to its life stage, as is the possibility of a
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) being asleep if
encountered in its lair. Note that even a wakeful
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) may appear to be
sleeping.

All [dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) can sense
hidden and invisible creatures within 6". From adulthood they are
impervious to [normal
missiles](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#normal-missiles) and need
never check
[morale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks).
Old and ancient [dragons](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons)
require [normal-types](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#normal-types)
to throw a positive
[morale](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#reaction-and-morale-checks)
check to approach nearer than 15" or to hold their ground if the
[dragon](http://ddo.immersiveink.com/dd.html#dragons) attacks.

##### Sleeping Dragons
